## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Registration and Execution

## Your Task

Trace how HTTP filter chains are registered and executed in the Envoy proxy. Find C++ and protobuf files across envoyproxy/envoy and envoyproxy/data-plane-api that implement: the FilterChainFactory interface (in envoy/http/), the FilterChainHelper that constructs chains from config, the FilterManager that executes filter chains at runtime, and the HttpConnectionManager proto that defines the filter_chain configuration schema.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

62-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of HTTP filter chain registration and execution in Envoy. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified

**Core Interfaces (envoy/http/):**
1. **FilterChainFactory** - Abstract interface for creating HTTP filter chains with `createFilterChain()` and `createUpgradeFilterChain()` methods
2. **FilterChainManager** - Sink interface where filter factories register their filters via `applyFilterFactoryCb()`
3. **FilterChainFactoryCallbacks** - Callbacks that filter factories use to add decoders, encoders, and access log handlers

**Implementation Classes (source/common/http/):**
1. **FilterManager** - Executes filter chains at runtime, managing filter lifecycle
2. **DownstreamFilterManager** - Specialized FilterManager with local reply handling
3. **FilterChainHelper** - Template class that processes filter configs and creates factory callbacks
4. **FilterChainUtility** - Helper utility that constructs filter chains from factory lists

**HTTP Connection Manager (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/):**
1. **HttpConnectionManagerConfig** - Implements FilterChainFactory, processes protobuf config
2. **ConnectionManagerImpl** - Network filter that creates streams and triggers filter chain setup

**Protocol Buffers (data-plane-api):**
1. **HttpConnectionManager** (v3 and v2) - Defines filter_chains configuration schema

## Execution Flow
Configuration → FilterChainHelper processes proto → FilterFactoryCb callbacks created → ConnectionManagerImpl creates streams → FilterManager calls callbacks → Filters instantiated and executed

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and detailed narrative explanation.

with configuration in protobuf definitions. The `HttpConnectionManager` message is defined in both v3 (`envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto`) and v2 (`envoy/config/filter/network/http_connection_manager/v2/http_connection_manager.proto`) versions. These proto messages contain the `filter_chains` field that defines which HTTP filters should be applied to incoming requests.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainFactory` interface (in `envoy/http/filter_factory.h`) is the abstract base for creating HTTP filter chains. It defines two main methods:\\n- `createFilterChain()`: Called when a new HTTP stream is created on the connection\\n- `createUpgradeFilterChain()`: Called when a new upgrade stream is created\\n\\nThe concrete implementation of `FilterChainFactory` is provided by `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` (in `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h`). This class inherits from both `Http::FilterChainFactory` and `Http::ConnectionManagerConfig`, and it processes the protobuf configuration to build the filter chain.\\n\\n## Configuration Processing\\n\\nThe `FilterChainHelper` template class (in `source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h`) is responsible for processing filter configurations at initialization time. It takes the `HttpFilter` messages from the proto configuration and creates `FilterFactoryCb` callbacks for each filter. The `FilterChainUtility` class (also in `filter_chain_helper.h`) provides the static method `createFilterChainForFactories()` which orchestrates the creation of the filter chain from a list of factory callbacks.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainManager` interface (in `envoy/http/filter_factory.h`) acts as the \\\"sink\\\" where filter factories can post their filters. The main method is `applyFilterFactoryCb()` which accepts a `FilterContext` and a `FilterFactoryCb` callback.\\n\\nThe `FilterFactoryCb` is a function type that takes `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks&` as a parameter. Individual filter factories return these callbacks during initialization, which are then called at stream creation time.\\n\\n## Execution Phase\\n\\nAt runtime, when a new HTTP stream is created, the `ConnectionManagerImpl` (in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`) - which implements the `Network::ReadFilter` interface - triggers filter chain creation by calling `createFilterChain()` on the configured `FilterChainFactory` (HttpConnectionManagerConfig). \\n\\nThe `FilterManager` class (in `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`) is responsible for executing the filter chain at runtime. It maintains the state of stream filters and manages their lifecycle. The `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` method calls the factory callbacks to instantiate the actual filter objects.\\n\\nThe `DownstreamFilterManager` (in `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`) extends `FilterManager` with explicit handling for sending local replies to the client.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` interface (in `envoy/http/filter.h`) provides the callbacks that filter factories use to add their filters to the chain:\\n- `addStreamDecoderFilter()`: Adds filters that process incoming request data\\n- `addStreamEncoderFilter()`: Adds filters that process outgoing response data\\n- `addStreamFilter()`: Adds bidirectional filters\\n- `addAccessLogHandler()`: Adds access log handlers\\n- `dispatcher()`: Provides access to the thread-local dispatcher\\n\\n## Complete Flow\\n\\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Protobuf config specifies filter_chains in HttpConnectionManager message\\n2. **Initialization**: HttpConnectionManagerConfig and FilterChainHelper process the config and create FilterFactoryCb callbacks\\n3. **Stream Creation**: When a new HTTP stream arrives, ConnectionManagerImpl calls HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()\\n4. **Filter Instantiation**: FilterManager calls the FilterFactoryCb callbacks which invoke FilterChainFactoryCallbacks::addStreamDecoderFilter/Encoder/Filter()\\n5. **Runtime Execution**: FilterManager orchestrates the execution of the filter chain, passing data through each filter in sequence\\n\\nThe key architectural pattern is the use of factory callbacks (`FilterFactoryCb`) that are created at configuration time but called at stream creation time. This allows for efficient filter instantiation with proper lifecycle management while maintaining separation between configuration and stream-specific behavior.\"\n}\n",

with configuration in protobuf definitions. The `HttpConnectionManager` message is defined in both v3 (`envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto`) and v2 (`envoy/config/filter/network/http_connection_manager/v2/http_connection_manager.proto`) versions. These proto messages contain the `filter_chains` field that defines which HTTP filters should be applied to incoming requests.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainFactory` interface (in `envoy/http/filter_factory.h`) is the abstract base for creating HTTP filter chains. It defines two main methods:\\n- `createFilterChain()`: Called when a new HTTP stream is created on the connection\\n- `createUpgradeFilterChain()`: Called when a new upgrade stream is created\\n\\nThe concrete implementation of `FilterChainFactory` is provided by `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` (in `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h`). This class inherits from both `Http::FilterChainFactory` and `Http::ConnectionManagerConfig`, and it processes the protobuf configuration to build the filter chain.\\n\\n## Configuration Processing\\n\\nThe `FilterChainHelper` template class (in `source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h`) is responsible for processing filter configurations at initialization time. It takes the `HttpFilter` messages from the proto configuration and creates `FilterFactoryCb` callbacks for each filter. The `FilterChainUtility` class (also in `filter_chain_helper.h`) provides the static method `createFilterChainForFactories()` which orchestrates the creation of the filter chain from a list of factory callbacks.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainManager` interface (in `envoy/http/filter_factory.h`) acts as the \\\"sink\\\" where filter factories can post their filters. The main method is `applyFilterFactoryCb()` which accepts a `FilterContext` and a `FilterFactoryCb` callback.\\n\\nThe `FilterFactoryCb` is a function type that takes `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks&` as a parameter. Individual filter factories return these callbacks during initialization, which are then called at stream creation time.\\n\\n## Execution Phase\\n\\nAt runtime, when a new HTTP stream is created, the `ConnectionManagerImpl` (in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`) - which implements the `Network::ReadFilter` interface - triggers filter chain creation by calling `createFilterChain()` on the configured `FilterChainFactory` (HttpConnectionManagerConfig). \\n\\nThe `FilterManager` class (in `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`) is responsible for executing the filter chain at runtime. It maintains the state of stream filters and manages their lifecycle. The `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` method calls the factory callbacks to instantiate the actual filter objects.\\n\\nThe `DownstreamFilterManager` (in `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`) extends `FilterManager` with explicit handling for sending local replies to the client.\\n\\nThe `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` interface (in `envoy/http/filter.h`) provides the callbacks that filter factories use to add their filters to the chain:\\n- `addStreamDecoderFilter()`: Adds filters that process incoming request data\\n- `addStreamEncoderFilter()`: Adds filters that process outgoing response data\\n- `addStreamFilter()`: Adds bidirectional filters\\n- `addAccessLogHandler()`: Adds access log handlers\\n- `dispatcher()`: Provides access to the thread-local dispatcher\\n\\n## Complete Flow\\n\\n1. **Configuration Loading**: Protobuf config specifies filter_chains in HttpConnectionManager message\\n2. **Initialization**: HttpConnectionManagerConfig and FilterChainHelper process the config and create FilterFactoryCb callbacks\\n3. **Stream Creation**: When a new HTTP stream arrives, ConnectionManagerImpl calls HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()\\n4. **Filter Instantiation**: FilterManager calls the FilterFactoryCb callbacks which invoke FilterChainFactoryCallbacks::addStreamDecoderFilter/Encoder/Filter()\\n5. **Runtime Execution**: FilterManager orchestrates the execution of the filter chain, passing data through each filter in sequence\\n\\nThe key architectural pattern is the use of factory callbacks (`FilterFactoryCb`) that are created at configuration time but called at stream creation time. This allows for efficient filter instantiation with proper lifecycle management while maintaining separation between configuration and stream-specific behavior.\"\n}\n",
